target=\&q;_blank\&q;&g;basic programming concepts&l;/a&g; such as variables, conditions and loops.&l;/li&g;&l;/ul&g;&q;,&q;seo_keywords&q;:&q;&q;,&q;selling_points&q;:{&q;images_url&q;:[],&q;selling_keys&q;:[]},&q;short_summary&q;:&q;Become a Front-End Web Developer by completing a variety of projects for your portfolio - become an HTML, CSS and JavaScript pro!&q;,&q;slug&q;:&q;front-end-web-developer-nanodegree--nd001&q;,&q;starter&q;:false,&q;student_groups&q;:[&q;6470958367637504&q;,&q;5937322874634240&q;,&q;5722516083179520&q;,&q;6085733720522752&q;,&q;5603432624553984&q;,&q;5442251091869696&q;,&q;5294184459927552&q;,&q;5501032782888960&q;,&q;5495837898309632&q;,&q;5809693463937024&q;,&q;6027070057218048&q;,&q;6295704985927680&q;,&q;6115407396864000&q;,&q;4943076007870464&q;,&q;4565995445026816&q;,&q;4947503859105792&q;,&q;6301558198501376&q;,&q;4857850135576576&q;,&q;5287759525969920&q;,&q;5436761678544896&q;,&q;6722477608927232&q;,&q;6715958364471296&q;,&q;6023498764124160&q;,&q;6256644858314752&q;,&q;5368165068701696&q;,&q;4512575093473280&q;,&q;5228759094919168&q;,&q;4983755399233536&q;,&q;6267327280054272&q;,&q;4817353793077248&q;,&q;6098424593645568&q;,&q;5841136825925632&q;,&q;4777828886773760&q;,&q;5644481010860032&q;,&q;5814728842018816&q;,&q;bd-nd001-students&q;],&q;subtitle&q;:&q;Become a Front End Developer&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;&q;,&q;syllabus&q;:&q;&l;p&g;The Front End Developer Nanodegree program is composed of eight projects. With each project, you&a;#39;ll create something that demonstrates your mastery of in-demand skills. Projects range in complexity, and each builds upon the previous. In the end, you will have a resume-worthy portfolio that you can showcase to prospective employers&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;PROJECT Mockup to Article&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;In this project, you&a;#39;ll be given a design mockup that you will convert into a website built with HTML. You will carefully examine the mockup to determine the specific tags to use to achieve the correct visual and structural result.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;PROJECT Animal Trading Cards&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;In this project, you will create a trading card for your favorite animal. You will use your knowledge of HTML to create the structure for your trading card. Then you will use CSS styling to design your trading card.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;PROJECT Build a Portfolio Site&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;For this project, you will build a portfolio website. You will be provided a design mockup as a PDF file, and you will replicate that design in HTML and CSS. You will develop a responsive website that will display images, descriptions, and links to each of the portfolio projects you will complete through the course of your Nanodegree program on any size screen.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;PROJECT Pixel Art Maker&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;In this project, you will build a single-page web application that allows users to draw pixel art on a customizable canvas. You&a;#39;ll be given starter code, including HTML and CSS, to build the application. You&a;#39;ll then use your JavaScript and jQuery skills to manipulate the DOM, allowing users to create a digital masterpiece!&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;PROJECT Memory Game&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;In this project, you will demonstrate your mastery of HTML, CSS, and JavaScript by building a complete browser-based card matching game (also known as Concentration). From building a grid of cards, adding functionality to handle user input, and implementing gameplay logic—you&a;#39;ll combine all your web development skills to create a fully interactive experience for your users.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;PROJECT Classic Arcade Game Clone&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;In this project, you’ll recreate the classic arcade game Frogger. You will be provided visual assets and a game loop engine; using these tools you willadd a number of entities to the game including the player characters and enemies. &l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;PROJECT Feed Reader Testing&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;In this project, you will learn about testing with Javascript. Many organizations practice a standard known as &a;quot;test-driven development&a;quot; or TDD, in which developers write tests first, before developing their application. Whether you work in an organization that writes tests extensively to inform product development or one that uses tests to encourage iteration, testing has become an essential skill in modern web development!&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;PROJECT Neighborhood Map&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;In this project, you will develop a single-page application featuring a neighborhood map. You will then add additional functionality, including: map markers to identify popular locations, a search function, and a listview to support simple browsing. You will remotely access JSON files containing restaurant information (including name, a photograph, address, cuisine type and operating hours) as well as JSON files containing review information for each restaurant (name of reviewer, date of review, 5-star rating and comments). When viewing a specific restaurant, current reviews must be displayed along with a form for the user to submit their own review.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;image&q;:&q;&q;,&q;index&q;:&q;&q;,&q;name&q;:&q;Project 3: Restaurant Reviewer&q;,&q;short_summary&q;:&q;&q;,&q;supporting_courses&q;:null}],&q;related_degree_keys&q;:[],&q;required_knowledge&q;:&q;&l;p&g;Students should know HTML, CSS, and JavaScript.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;seo_keywords&q;:&q;&q;,&q;selling_points&q;:{&q;images_url&q;:null,&q;selling_keys&q;:null},&q;short_summary&q;:&q;Get hands-on experience making web applications accessible. You’ll understand when and why users need accessibility, then you’ll dive into how to implement.&q;,&q;slug&q;:&q;web-accessibility--ud891&q;,&q;starter&q;:false,&q;student_groups&q;:[],&q;subtitle&q;:&q;Developing with Empathy&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;&l;p&g;In this course you’ll get hands-on experience making web applications accessible. You’ll understand when and why users need accessibility. Then you’ll dive into the \&q;how\&q;: making a page work properly with screen readers, and managing input focus (e.g. the highlight you see when tabbing through a form.) You’ll understand what \&q;semantics\&q; and \&q;semantic markup\&q; mean for web pages and add ARIA markup to enable navigating the interface with a range of assistive devices. Finally, you’ll learn styling techniques that help users with partial vision navigate your pages easily and reliably.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;This course is also featured in our &l;a href=\&q;/course/full-stack-web-developer-nanodegree--nd004\&q;&g;Senior Web Developer Nanodegree&l;/a&g; program.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;syllabus&q;:&q;&l;h2&g;Lesson 1: Overview&l;/h2&g;&l;p&g;In this lesson you’ll learn why accessibility matters, and who it affects. You’ll also get a first look at the web accessibility guidelines (WAI – Web Accessibility Initiative), understand what \&q;POUR\&q; means for accessibility, and locate checklists to help make your own sites accessible.&l;/p&g;&l;h2&g;Lesson 2: Focus&l;/h2&g;&l;p&g;In this lesson you’ll learn how to make a page usable for anyone navigating with the keyboard. This starts with an introduction to the concept of focus (the element on the page to which keyboard events will be targeted), how to make elements focusable and when, and the order in which focusable elements will be traversed when exploring the page with the keyboard. You’ll also learn how to manage focus in forms, in custom components, pop-ups, and off-screen content. &l;/p&g;&l;h2&g;Lesson 3: Semantics Basics&l;/h2&g;&l;p&g;In this lesson you’ll build on keyboard navigation to make a page work for people who are unable to use a standard user interface, including users who can&a;#39;t see the screen. This requires ensuring assistive technology (such as screen readers) has sufficient information to present an alternative UI. You’ll use a screen reader to try out ordinary form elements and add markup to make them work even better. You’ll understand the accessibility tree the browser constructs from the DOM. Finally, you’ll learn how to built-in HTML features to ensure the accessibility tree accurately reflects the visual UI. &l;/p&g;&l;h2&g;Lesson 4: Semantics Extras&l;/h2&g;&l;p&g;In this lesson, you’ll dive deeper into the screen-reader experience to add hyper-fast navigation. You’ll learn how to arrange headings and label links so screen reader users can fly through your pages! You’ll also learn how to call out \&q;landmarks\&q; into your page to speed up navigation even more. (As a bonus, this \&q;semantic markup\&q;  also makes your markup more readable!)&l;/p&g;&l;h2&g;Lesson 5: Semantics - ARIA&l;/h2&g;&l;p&g;In this lesson, you’ll move beyond the native elements of HTML into building custom controls and interactions. Of course you want these to be accessible, and that’s where ARIA comes in – Accessible Rich Internet Applications. You’ll learn how to add attributes to your custom interactions to make them as accessible as native elements. You’ll also learn how to manage these attributes from Javascript as the user interacts with your page.&l;/p&g;&l;h2&g;Lesson 6: Style&l;/h2&g;&l;p&g;In this lesson, you’ll learn the third pillar of Accessibility (after Focus and Semantics): Styling. Your page’s styles need to support highlighting the focus, indicating ARIA states, being zoomed in or out, and viewed by people with limited color or contrast vision. You’ll learn how to audit your page with the Chrome Accessibility Tools and correct any styling issues that pop up, as well as designing with accessibility in mind.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;tags&q;:[&q;css&q;,&q;html&q;,&q;javascript&q;],&q;teaser_video&q;:{&q;transcodings&q;:{&q;480p_1000kbps_mp4&q;:{},&q;480p_mp4&q;:{},&q;480p_ogg&q;:{},&q;720p_mp4&q;:{}}},&q;title&q;:&q;Web Accessibility&q;,&q;tracks&q;:[&q;All&q;,&q;Web Development&q;],&q;why_nd_summary&q;:&q;&q;,&q;why_nd_data&q;:&q;&q;},{&q;affiliates&q;:[{&q;image&q;:&q;https://s3-us-west-1.amazonaws.com/udacity-content/partner/logo-color-google-1c8cf8f.svg&q;,&q;key&q;:&q;google&q;,&q;name&q;:&q;Google&q;}],&q;apply_required&q;:false,&q;available&q;:true,&q;banner_image&q;:&q;https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/yDK0u2UV6duS3-Y2VRRs94CBRHnRkk2w5Os5jdF6tPQXxz5NGSm1Tyy9eUQdvZluagt1xpRMWXoZuj7v1w=s0#w=4680&a;h=968&q;,&q;capped&q;:false,&q;enables_profiles&q;:false,&q;expected_duration&q;:2,&q;expected_duration_high&q;:0,&q;expected_duration_low&q;:2,&q;expected_duration_unit&q;:&q;weeks&q;,&q;expected_learning&q;:&q;&l;p&g;The modern web is mobile and interactive. Thousands (maybe millions?) of websites include account creation forms and checkout forms. Websites ask you to tap buttons and fill out text boxes. They ask you for information and prompt you to take action. You fill out forms on big screens with physical keyboards and small screens with virtual keyboards.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;There are millions of ways users interact with the modern web, and any website with interactions needs to do everything it can to influence the way users interact in order to ultimately increase conversions.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;Building High Conversion Web Forms exists to help you, the web developer, think about forms and interactions for all of your users, no matter the form or the device. You&a;#39;ll practice handling user input to build forms that rock!&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;faq&q;:&q;&q;,&q;featured&q;:false,&q;features&q;:null,&q;full_course_available&q;:false,&q;graduate_groups&q;:[],&q;hero_video&q;:&q;&q;,&q;hero_video_poster&q;:&q;&q;,&q;hero_video_id&q;:&q;&q;,&q;hiring_affiliates&q;:null,&q;image&q;:&q;https://d20vrrgs8k4bvw.cloudfront.net/images/courses/thumbnails/ud890_thumbnail.jpg&q;,&q;instructors&q;:[{&q;bio&q;:&q;&l;p&g;Ido is a Developer Advocate for Google Chrome. Learn how to design and build web forms for users on any device.&q;,&q;slug&q;:&q;building-high-conversion-web-forms--ud890&q;,&q;starter&q;:false,&q;student_groups&q;:[],&q;subtitle&q;:&q;Forms Rock!&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;&l;p&g;Any meaningful experience on the web has a form. Whether it&a;#39;s a form made of text boxes, toggles, buttons, checkboxes, or touchable widgets, web developers need to be purposeful about forms to make users happy and increase &l;a href=\&q;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conversion_marketing\&q;&g;conversions&l;/a&g;.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;In this course, you&a;#39;ll learn best practices for modern forms as taught by Google&a;#39;s Ido Green and Udacity&a;#39;s Cameron Pittman. You&a;#39;ll practice your skills along the way with a few self-directed projects, including an e-commerce checkout and an event planner app!&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;As a special treat, you&a;#39;ll also watch a series of interviews with Luke Wroblewski, Google Product Director and author of &l;a href=\&q;http://www.lukew.com/resources/web_form_design.asp\&q;&g;Web Form Design&l;/a&g;, to get his take on interactions for the modern web.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;syllabus&q;:&q;&l;h3&g;Efficient Inputs Part 1&l;/h3&g;&l;ul&g;&l;li&g;You&a;#39;ll be introduced to the principles of useful forms&l;/li&g;&l;li&g;You&a;#39;ll research HTML5 input types&l;/li&g;&l;li&g;You&a;#39;ll build a datalist input&l;/li&g;&l;/ul&g;&l;h3&g;Efficient Inputs Part 2&l;/h3&g;&l;ul&g;&l;li&g;You&a;#39;ll exercise best practices for implementing input labels and types with many sample inputs&l;/li&g;&l;li&g;You&a;#39;ll validate user input with HTML5 attributes and the &l;a href=\&q;https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/Guide/HTML/Forms_in_HTML#Constraint_Validation_API\&q;&g;Constraint Validation API&l;/a&g;&l;/li&g;&l;/ul&g;&l;h3&g;Fast Forms&l;/h3&g;&l;ul&g;&l;li&g;You&a;#39;ll start exploring techniques for making forms faster and easier for users&l;/li&g;&l;li&g;You&a;#39;ll practice empathy for your users in order to simplify and expedite forms&l;/li&g;&l;li&g;You&a;#39;ll apply everything you&a;#39;ve learned so far by designing and building an e-commerce checkout&l;/li&g;&l;/ul&g;&l;h3&g;Touch Support&l;/h3&g;&l;ul&g;&l;li&g;You&a;#39;ll explore best practices for responding to and designing user interactions on mobile&l;/li&g;&l;li&g;You&a;#39;ll use touch events to build a mobile-ready touch slider&l;/li&g;&l;li&g;You&a;#39;ll be introduced to the final project -
